```markdown
# Yuan Ze University International Competition Subsidy Regulations for Art and Design

Approved at the 8th Academic Affairs Meeting of 2022 academic year on July 12, 2023   
Amended and approved at the 1th Academic Affairs Meeting of 2024 academic year on Sept 18, 2024

## Article I: Objective

In order to enhance the positive performance of our students in international design competitions, encourage students to participate in international art and design competitions, broaden their international horizons, and further promote the competitiveness of this University, these Regulations have been thus formulated, and they are applied from the implementation of the second phase of the Higher Education Intensive Cultivation Program of the Ministry of Education.

## Article II: Eligibility for Grant Application

1. Undergraduate and graduate students from this University.

2. Students must be a member who has participated in and completed the training of the “Yuan Ze University Secretss for Winning the International Design Competition - Design Workshop” organized by this University.

## Article III: Grant Items

The works applied for must be mainly in the name of Yuan Ze University to participate in the competitions, and no other unit shall participate in the competitions in the name of co-creators. The grant items and amounts are as follows:

1. Subsidies will be provided to individual students or groups for registration fees and enrollment fees for participating in international competitions, with a maximum limit of NT\$5,000. Each work is limited to one application.

2. Overseas shipping and mailing fees for works are limited to NT\$1,000 per piece.

3. The “International Competition for Art and Design” announced by the Ministry of Education will be as a priority subsidy project for those participating in the international competitions.

4. The funding for competition participation as outlined in these regulations will be supported by the Higher Education Sprout Project (MOE) budget for the current year. When the allocated funds for the year are exhausted, a public announcement will be made to suspend the subsidy program.

## Article IV: Application Procedures

The applicant must submit all relevant information and proofs to the Centre for Teaching Excellence for reimbursement within two weeks after the competition ended (within the same accounting year).

## 1. Application form

2. Brief description or brochure of the activity

3. Documents to prove participation in the competition

4. Receipts and vouchers for the relevant expenditure of participating in the competition should be attached, and the content of the official receipts should include the name of the competition, the name of the work, and the fee

Article V: Obligations of the Creator

1. The creator shall be responsible for defending and explaining the content of his/her work during the application process of the competition, and shall assist the University to carry out the necessary procedures without compensation.

2. The creator shall be responsible for any infringement of the rights of others due to plagiarism or other unlawful means.

## Article VI: Others

Applicants who receive subsidies under these Regulations are obliged to provide posters, animations and other relevant achievement materials in the future. Non-exclusive authorization is granted to this University for all use of publications, displays and database systems in order to facilitate the presentation of this University’s academic achievements.

Article VII: These Regulations shall be implemented after they are approved by the Academic Affairs Meeting, and the same applies to any amendments.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Course Offering and Scheduling Guidelines

Passed by the 6th Academic Affairs Meeting, Academic Year 2023, on April 19, 2023

Revised by the 7th Academic Affairs Meeting, Academic Year 2023, on March 20, 2024

Revised by the 8th Academic Affairs Meeting, Academic Year 2023, on May 1, 2024

Revised by the 9th Academic Affairs Meeting, Academic Year 2023, on June 5, 2024

Article 1. This guideline has been established to provide a reference for all course-offering units to follow when offering and scheduling courses.

Article 2. The principle of course offering:

1. Each unit should consider the following factors when planning a course: a long-term perspective, necessity, feasibility, graduation requirements for students, availability of teaching resources, and obtaining approval from the relevant curriculum committee.

2. The course planning should include the course name in both Chinese and English, syllabus, offering unit, course type, and credits.

3. The lecture hours should correspond to the course credits, except for special courses such as physical education, laboratory classes, internships, and capstone projects.

4. Courses should meet the minimum number of students: 15 students in the undergraduate courses, 5 students in the master's courses, and 3 students in the doctoral courses. Compulsory courses are not subject to the limit on the number of students. Elective courses that have reached 2/3 of the minimum enrollment limit, the course offering unit may consider whether to continue. Compulsory course for small class teaching with two or more classes (inclusive) and the number of students does not reach the minimum limit must be signed and approved by the Dean of Students.

5. The lecture hours for each semester must not be fewer than 18 weeks.

6. The teacher should complete the course proposal, submit a self-assessment, and obtain approval from the department before the course selection period.

7. If a course requires a change in course name and credits, it will be treated as a new course. In such cases, please submit a syllabus of course and obtain approval from the relevant curriculum committee.

8. It is recommended to assign a full-time teacher to teach the required subjects, except for special courses.

9. If there are special circumstances that require courses to be taught during the summer vacation, they will be considered as courses for the following semester.

10. After the announcement of courses for each semester, individuals who wish to make course changes are required to complete a Course Change Application Form.

## Article 3. The principle of course scheduling:

1. For undergraduate core required courses, the International Language and Culture Center,

Physical Education Office, and College of General Studies have priority in scheduling courses. Other course-offering units are not allowed to schedule professional subjects during those time.

2. Short-term intensive completion of the entire semester's courses is not allowed.

3. On Mondays, Tuesdays, Thursdays, and Fridays, one-hour courses are recommended to be scheduled during the first, sixth, and tenth sessions. Two-hour courses should not be scheduled during the second to third sessions or the seventh to eighth sessions, while threehour courses should not be scheduled during the seventh to ninth sessions.

4. The sixth session on Wednesdays is designated as teacher time and should not be scheduled for classes. One-hour courses are recommended to be scheduled during the first, seventh, and tenth sessions, while two-hour courses should not be scheduled during the second to third sessions or the eighth to ninth sessions.

5. The principle of course scheduling for college and graduate school:

a. The daily course schedule should not exceed 10 sessions. Special courses can apply for additional teaching time.

b. Consecutive teaching of the same course should not exceed four sessions. Special courses can apply for additional teaching time. E.g. medical internship, art and music performance practice courses, practical courses or hiring foreign scholars and experts and other special properties.

c. Master's degree courses (excluding in-service master's degree courses), such as Open University students, are limited to third-year students or above in the day department and post-baccalaureate students. In-service master courses are available for post-baccalaureate students.

6. The course schedule for the Master's In-Service Program is primarily in the evenings from Monday to Friday, with Saturdays and Sundays as supplementary.

Article 4. For any matters not covered by the regulations, will be handled in accordance with the Study Regulation and other relevant provisions.

Article 5. The " Yuan Ze University Course Offering and Scheduling Guidelines" have been approved by the Academic Affairs Meeting and implemented afterwards.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Regulations for the Implementation of Teaching Assistant System

Approved at the 4th academic affairs meeting of the 2007 academic Year on Mar.12, 2008

Amended at the 1st academic affairs meeting of the 2011 academic Year on Oct.5, 2011

Amended at the 1st academic affairs meeting of the 2015 academic Year on Sept.30, 2015

Amended and approved at the 1st academic affairs meeting of the 2023 academic year on Sept.27, 2023

Amended and approved at the 7th academic affairs meeting of the 2024 academic year on Mar.20, 2024

Article I In order to promote the teaching assistant system, to encourage outstanding students to serve as teaching assistants, to help teachers improve the quality of teaching, to strengthen the learning effectiveness of students, and to ensure the rights and obligations of the teaching assistants, these Regulations has been formulated in accordance with the “Yuan Ze University Management Guidelines for Students Working as Part-time Teaching Assistants”.

Article II The qualifications for working as teaching assistants are as follows:

1. Graduate students of master’s and doctoral programs, and graduate students of master’s in-service programs with excellent academic performance and good conduct.

2. Students in the third to fourth years of the undergraduate program with excellent academic performance and good conduct.

Students who meet one of the two qualifications listed above will be given priority in hiring upon approval by the teaching faculty and the course provider. If it is necessary to hire a student in the second year or below of a bachelor’s degree program as a teaching assistant, the teaching unit will propose and discuss the proposal at a departmental meeting for approval before the appointment is made.

Article III The definitions, types, and job descriptions of teaching assistants stated in these Regulations are as follows:

Teaching assistants are those students who are studying in the University and are hired to assist teachers in teaching activities, production of teaching materials, group experiments or internships, classroom counseling services, grading and registering of homework papers, and proctoring of exams, and other teaching-related matters, in order to enhance the quality of teaching. Teaching assistants are not allowed to be asked by teachers to engage in non-teaching related activities or to teach on behalf of teachers, except for assisting in teaching activities.

1. Learning-based Part-time Teaching Assistant: This is defined as a part-time teaching assistant who is employed in a program of course learning or service learning where learning is the primary purpose and area of study, which is a non-reciprocal employment relationship.

2. Labor-based Part-time Teaching Assistant:. This refers to the fact that both parties have a reciprocal employment relationship in which labor is provided for remuneration.

The types of teaching activities include general courses, laboratory courses, digital teaching courses, and language courses. Teaching assistants’ work is related to course work, service learning, and

after-school remediation.

Regulations for Teaching Assistants in Teaching Units

Article IV Each academic unit shall, depending on the needs of professional courses and subsidized funds, formulate the “Enforcement Rules for Teaching Assistants” of each academic unit and refer to the definition, type, and job description of teaching assistants in Article 3 to handle the matters related to the allocation, treatment, personnel, and work evaluation of teaching assistants. The relevant regulations will be sent to each college for approval after discussion in the unit meeting.

Article V The rights and interests of part-time teaching assistants of the University shall be protected in accordance with the “Yuan Ze University Management Guidelines for Students Working as Part-time Teaching Assistants” and the relevant regulations of the University.

Article VI Learning-based part-time teaching assistants of the University must sign the “Yuan Ze University Part-Time Teaching Assistant Learning Agreement” with the University in order to receive scholarships or incentives.

Article VII Labor-based part-time teaching assistants of the University must sign the “Yuan Ze University Part-time Teaching Assistant Labor Contract” with the University in order to receive salary or work-study payment.

Article VIII Scholarships or incentives for learning-based part-time teaching assistants of the University and hourly wages or work-study payments for labor-based part-time teaching assistants of the University will be paid on a regular basis in accordance with the “Yuan Ze University Management Guidelines for Students Working as Part-time Teaching Assistants” of the University and the “Enforcement Rules for Teaching Assistants” of each academic unit of the University, as well as the relevant regulations of the academic and administrative units.

Article IX Students who work as teaching assistants are required to attend the Teaching Assistant Workshop organized by the Teaching Excellence Center for of the Office of Academic Affairs every semester.

Article X Each unit is responsible for evaluating the performance of teaching assistants, which will serve as the basis for incentives and reimbursement.

Article XI Teaching assistants are expected to behave as follows:

1. Accept the supervision and guidance of the teacher and to assist the teacher in teaching.

2. Respect the teacher and the students by observing the ethical boundaries.

3. Adhere to the principle of fairness and impartiality, and ensure the privacy of the students. 4. Comply with the Gender Equality Education Act, the Gender Equality Work Act, and the relevant regulations of the University.

Article XII These Regulations will be implemented after it has been approved by the Academic Affairs Meeting, and the same applies to any amendments. .
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Regulations Governing Incentives for Innovative Teaching

Approved at the 4th administrative affairs meeting of the 2023 academic year on Sept.20, 2023

Article I In order to establish the teaching characteristics of the University, to encourage teachers to enhance students’ learning interest and effectiveness through innovative teaching, and to recognize and reward teachers’ efforts and contributions in teaching, these regulations are formulated.

Article II Eligibility: Full-time faculty members who meet the minimum requirements of the “Teaching” category of the “Yuan Ze University Teacher Evaluation and Reward Regulations” and have participated in the University’s Higher Education Sprout Project are eligible to apply for the award.

Article III There are four types of award programs:

1) Special Merit Award for Innovative Teaching

2) Merit Award for Innovative Teaching

3) Innovative Teaching Honorable Mention Award

4) Award for Higher Education Sprout Implementation Project

## Article IV Application Procedures: The applicant shall submit the application form with related documents to the Office of Academic Affairs after approved by the supervisor of the unit he/she serves in. In addition, the unit of implementation of the relevant teaching program shall actively recommend candidate teachers and then submit their applications to the Office of Academic Affairs.

Article V The assessment criteria will be based on the following key points:

1. Innovation in Teaching

(i) Developing new and effective teaching methods

(ii) Promoting the wider use of learning resources by students

(iii) Providing solutions to teaching problems

2. Teaching Effectiveness

(i) Enhancing students’ willingness and ability to learn

(ii) Improvement of teaching strategies in the classroom

Article VI The review committee for innovative teaching award that consists of 5-7 committee members shall be established. The colleges may recommend one or two candidate teachers performing excellent in teaching respectively for application. Upon completion of initial review by the Office of Academic Affairs, the applications will be sent to the President for approval and the convener for reviewing their applications may be designated.

Article VII Review Procedures: A written review will be conducted based on the application information. If no applicants meet the approved standards, the award will be excused.

Article VIII Award content: Applicants will be evaluated according to the category of their application, and if the score of 80 points is not reached, the award will be excused.

1. Special Merit Award for Innovative Teaching: A prize of NT\$100,000 and a certificate of merit will be awarded.

2. Merit Award for Innovative Teaching: A prize of NT\$70,000 and a certificate of merit will be awarded.

3. Innovative Teaching Honorable Mention Award: A prize of NT\$40,000 and a certificate of merit will be awarded.

4. Award for Higher Education Sprout Implementation Project: A prize of NT\$20,000 and a certificate of merit will be awarded.

All of the above awards are subject to tax deduction in accordance with the tax law.

Article IX Obligations: Teachers who receive the Teaching Innovation Award are examples of innovative teaching in the University, and they are required to assist in the promotion of the Higher Education Sprout Project for responding to the needs of future development of the University by providing the following information:

1. Presenting their teaching experience in the relevant teaching seminars of the University and opening up the classroom of teachers in the University for teaching observation.

2. Within one month after the end of the award period, submit the related result materials (including teaching materials, lesson plans, handouts, teaching history and records, counseling records, service records, or award preparation materials) to the review committee for evaluation and review.

Article X The funding for the awards under these Regulations will be supported by the Ministry of Education’s Higher Education Sprout Project. All other matters will be handled in accordance with the relevant regulations of the Ministry of Education and the University. These regulations will be implemented after it has been approved by the administrative meeting, and the same applies to any amendments.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Regulations on Lecture Adjustments and Make-Up Lectures

Approved by the 8th Academic Affairs Meeting of the 2023 Academic Year on May 1st, 2024

Revised by the 2nd Academic Affairs Meeting of the 2024 Academic Year on November 20th, 2024

Revised by the 4th Academic Affairs Meeting of the 2024 Academic Year on April 23th, 2025

Article 1 To be followed by all full-time and part-time faculty members on lecture adjustments and make-up lectures, the “Regulations on Lecture Adjustments and Make-Up Lectures” have been established. (Hereinafter referred to as these regulations.)

Article 2 If lecturers are absent from a lecture due to taking a leave, they must apply make-up lectures in advance or arrange for substitute lectures. Lecturers should follow the provisions of Chapter 6 of the “YZU Regulations for Employment, Payment, Service of Faculties” and the “YZU Regulations Governing the Appointment of Adjunct Faculty,” and the leave procedures in accordance with the relevant regulations of the Personnel Office.

## Article 3 The rules of adjusting and making-up lectures

1. Unless there are special circumstances, lecturers must teach according to the original course schedule.

2. If lecturers need to adjust or make-up lectures of elective courses, they must notify the students in advance.

3. Lecture adjustments and make-up lectures must be applied in advance through the school curriculum system, and all students in the course must be notified.

4. The head or supervisor of the course-offering department should review the rationality and necessity of the lecturers’ applications for lecture adjustments and make-up lectures, and urge the lecturers to complete the procedures.

5. The lecture adjustments and make-up lectures shall not affect the rights and interests of other lecturers and students of the courses.

6. The time of the make-up lectures shall not exceed four hours beyond the scheduled teaching time on the same day.

7. In order to protect students’ rights of taking examinations, there shall be no makeup lectures during midterm and final examination weeks.

8. In order to protect students’ rights of receiving education, if midterm and final examinations are moved to other weeks, lecturers must teach on the midterm and final examination weeks.

9. The time of the make-up lectures is based on the class sections. It is recommended to give priority to arrange make-up lectures the sixth section on Wednesday. Please note that the sixth section on Wednesday is also the tutor time.

10. If the make-up lectures are scheduled between 12PM and 1PM, the lecturer must confirm with the students and secure the time for taking meals.

11. On lecture adjustments and make-up lectures, the lecturers must provide supplement materials and relevant resources for the affected students, such as recorded videos of the lectures, to protect students’ right of receiving education.

12. After lecture adjustments and make-up lectures, relevant certificates must be submitted for review by the head or supervisor of the course-offering department.

## Article 4 In the event of a disaster, if faculty or students are affected due to residing in or commuting through areas where government-mandated work and class suspensions are in effect, while Taoyuan City has not issued a similar suspension, flexible teaching measures may be implemented to prioritize safety and safeguard students' right to education.

1. Faculty may employ synchronous remote teaching or provide course materials, handouts, or other flexible measures as appropriate to the course. These measures should ensure that students' learning is not disrupted, and faculty should promptly notify their supervisors and inform students accordingly.

2. Students must notify their instructors immediately and follow the required procedures to apply for leave. If needed, they may request support from instructors in accessing online classes or relevant materials.

3. If an instructor cannot conduct the class in any manner during the scheduled session, they must inform their supervisors without delay and communicate the necessary updates to the students. Subsequent arrangements shall be made in line with these guidelines.

Article 5 The matters not covered by these regulations shall be implemented in accordance with Academic Regulations and other regulations of the university.

Article 6 These regulations and their revisions shall be passed by Academic Affairs Meeting and then implemented on the date of promulgation.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Regulations Governing Incentives for Outstanding Teaching Assistant in English-Taught Program

Approved at the 9th academic affairs meeting of the 2023 academic year on Jun.5, 2024

Article I In order to recognize the contribution of teaching assistants to the English-Taught Program (including EMI courses) and encourage teaching assistants with outstanding performance to demonstrate their teaching enthusiasm and skills and to attain the goals of enhancing the teaching quality of teaching assistants in the English-Taught Program (including EMI courses), the “Outstanding Teaching Assistant Award in English-Taught Program” is established.

## Article II Selection Candidates

1. Serving as teaching assistants in the EMI courses for the academic year who are responsible for assisting teachers in teaching or leading students to conduct discussions, experiments or counseling them, as well as evaluating grades and other affairs relating to assisting teaching staffs and interacting with students.

2. Serving as teaching assistants in the English-Taught Program for the academic year who are responsible for assisting teachers in teaching or leading students to conduct discussions, experiments or counseling them, as well as evaluating grades and other affairs relating to assisting teaching staffs and interacting with students.

## Article III Selection Timetable:

Applications will be accepted from the second semester of each academic year:

1. Teaching assistants for courses offered by the focused incubation colleges should submit their applications to the bilingual enter of each college. Each college will select outstanding teaching assistants from among them respectively, and after examination by the universitylevel bilingual center, the outstanding teaching assistants will be publicly commended at the end of the semester.

2. Teaching assistants for courses offered by the non-focused incubation colleges and other teaching units should submit their applications to the university-level bilingual center. After reviewing them, each teaching unit will select outstanding teaching assistants from among them respectively, the outstanding teaching assistants will be publicly commended at the end of the semester.

## Article IV Criteria for Review:

1. A high degree of enthusiasm for the program, the ability to understand the needs of students, stimulate students’ interest in learning, and demonstrate excellent teaching skills.

2. Interacting well with teachers and students, effectively assisting teachers in compiling teaching materials and conducting classroom teaching activities, and evaluating grades fairly.

3. Providing after-school counseling, and students will make concrete progress through the counseling, and fulfill the duties of teaching assistants.

## Article V Evaluation Procedures:

The evaluation process is divided into two stages: recommendation and review.

1. Recommendation:

Nominated by each department (classes, groups, or the same level units affiliated to the college), the candidates for outstanding teaching assistants will be recommended by the

department (classes, groups, or the same level units affiliated to the college) according to the teacher’s assessment and recommendation forms.

## 2. Review

i) If applicants are from the focused incubation colleges, a written assessment will be conducted by the bilingual center of each college based on the above criteria for review. The outstanding teaching assistants will be publicly commended after the result is approved by the university-level bilingual center.

ii) If applicants are from the non-focused incubation colleges and other academic units will be assessed by the bilingual center of the Academic Affairs Office.

Article VI Rewards and Recognition: Those who do not meet the standards may be removed from the program.

According to the review results, one outstanding teaching assistant from each department (classes, groups, or the same level units affiliated to the college) will be selected and awarded with a certificate of appreciation and a cash prize of NT\$5,000, and will be publicly recognized.

Article VII The funding for the awards of these Regulations shall be supported by the Ministry of Education’s Program on Bilingual Education for Students in College. Matters not covered herein shall be handled in accordance with the relevant regulations of the Ministry of Education and the University

Article VIII These Regulations will be implemented after it is approved by the academic affairs meeting, and the same applies to any amendments.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Outstanding Teaching Award Guidelines for English-Medium Instruction (EMI) Courses

Approved at the 9th Academic Affairs Meeting of Academic Year 2023 on June 5, 2024

Amended at the 6th Academic Affairs Meeting of Academic Year 2024 on June 4, 2025

## Article 1

To encourage faculty participation in the Ministry of Education's “Bilingual Education for Students in College” initiative (hereinafter referred to as the “EMI Project”), to promote EMI course offerings, and to recognize the efforts and contributions of instructors teaching EMI and English-taught courses, Yuan Ze University (hereinafter referred to as “the University”) hereby establishes the “Outstanding Teaching Award Guidelines for English-Medium Instruction Courses” (hereinafter referred to as “the Guidelines”).

## Article 2 – Eligibility

1. Faculty members at the University who teach courses under the EMI Project.

2. Faculty members who teach in English (regardless of college affiliation) and meet the minimum teaching requirements under the “Yuan Ze University Faculty Evaluation and Reward Guidelines” are eligible to apply.

## Article 3 – Application Procedure

Applications may be submitted in one of the following ways:

1. The applicant submits the application form and relevant documents to their department. After approval by the department chair, the materials are forwarded to the Resource Center of EMI (RCEMI) under the Office of Academic Affairs.

2. The EMI project administrative office may recommend eligible candidates directly to the RCEMI.

## Article 4 – Review Committee

A Review Committee consisting of 5 to 7 members shall be formed. Colleges will nominate 1 to 3 outstanding instructors, and the RCEMI will compile nominations and seek approval from the Dean of Academic Affairs, who will also designate the committee convener.

Article 5 – Evaluation Criteria

Applications will be evaluated based on the following criteria:

1. Provision of in-class recording or online course link available on a public website

2. Participation in internal or external EMI-related professional development courses or activities

3. Openness to and acceptance of classroom observations by internal or external institutions

4. Enhancement of students’ motivation to learn in English

5. Improvement of students’ academic English proficiency

6. Classroom interaction and engagement with students

7. Innovation or improvement in teaching strategies

8. Promotion of students’ use of English-learning resources both on and off campus

Article 6 – Review Process

Applications will be reviewed through a document-based evaluation. Awards will not be granted if submissions do not meet the required standard.

Article 7 – Awards

1. Outstanding EMI Teaching Award: NT\$100,000 and a certificate

2. Excellent EMI Teaching Award: NT\$70,000 and a certificate

3. Meritorious EMI Teaching Award: NT\$40,000 and a certificate

4. EMI Project Implementation Award: NT\$20,000 and a certificate

All awards are subject to applicable tax deductions according to national tax regulations.

Article 8 – Obligations of Award Recipients

Award recipients serve as exemplary EMI instructors and are expected to support the EMI Project, including the following:

1. Recipients of Outstanding and Excellent Awards may not apply again within 3 years and must serve as mentors in the following academic year. They are to provide guidance and consultation to other EMI instructors at the University through various means, such as one-on-one mentoring, classroom observation, or other formats. Mentor-mentee matching is self-arranged.

2. Share teaching experience at EMI training workshops, teaching forums, or other related events organized by the University.

## Article 9 – Funding

All awards and associated costs are funded by the Ministry of Education’s “Bilingual Education for Students in College” initiative. Any matters not covered herein shall follow the relevant regulations of the Ministry of Education and the University.

## Article 10 – Implementation

These Guidelines shall take effect upon approval by the Academic Affairs Meeting. Amendments shall follow the same procedure.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Directives for the Establishment of the Artificial Intelligence Credit Program Committee

Approved by the 3rd Academic Affairs Meeting, Academic Year 2024, on December 25, 2024

## Article I

To address the pressing need for artificial intelligence (AI) talent in the industry and in alignment with the Ministry of Education’s Taiwan Artificial Intelligence College Alliance (hereinafter referred to as TAICA Alliance) initiative, Yuan Ze University establishes the Artificial Intelligence Credit Program Committee (hereinafter referred to as the Committee) to promote AI education. These directives are hereby formulated.

Article II The Committee shall be convened by the Dean of the Office of Academic Affairs, with deans of all colleges serving as ex-officio members. Additionally, each college shall nominate one faculty representative, and one representative each from the Office of Information Services and Innovation Center for Artificial Intelligence Applications shall also serve as members. The term of office for committee members is one year. Relevant units may be invited to attend meetings as necessary.

Article III The tasks of the Committee are as follows:

1. To execute matters related to the TAICA Alliance’s credit programs and other AI credit programs, including revising these directives, planning the course schedule for the credit programs, and coordinating responsible units within the University for each credit program under the TAICA Alliance.

2. To review and approve regular courses within the University: Based on the program planning documents provided by the TAICA Alliance Office, the Committee shall inventory and review courses eligible for recognition or process applications submitted by responsible units for course recognition. Courses approved by the TAICA Alliance Office will be added to the aforementioned credit program course schedule.

3. To plan satellite courses: The Committee shall assist in identifying potential course providers, coordinate with full-time and part-time faculty to offer satellite courses, and support teaching equipment, venues, and network communications.

4. To assist in the certification of student programs:

i) Student applications for internal credit programs and certificate issuance shall be processed in accordance with the University’s “Yuan Ze University Regulations for Establishing Academic Credit Programs.”

ii) Students applying for TAICA Alliance certification, if compliant with the Alliance’s requirements, shall be referred to the TAICA Alliance Office for issuance of the Ministry of Education TAICA Alliance digital certificate, which shall be submitted to the Committee for record-keeping.

5. To integrate the University’s cross-disciplinary AI course resources and facilitate matters related to cross-disciplinary AI credit programs.

Article IV The Committee may establish subcommittees as needed to fulfill its tasks. Meetings shall be held at least once per semester, with extraordinary meetings convened as necessary.

Article V These directives shall be implemented following approval by the Academic Affairs Meeting. Amendments shall follow the same procedure.

If any controversies or disputes occurred regarding clauses of the contract, it shall always refer to its Chinese version
```

```markdown
# Regulations for the Implementation of the Disciplinary Self-Directed Learning Project, Yuan Ze University

Approved at the 6th Academic Affairs Meeting of the 2024 Academic Year on June 4, 2025

Article 1 To promote student-centered learning and encourage students to integrate their academic disciplines with self-directed learning, aiming to cultivate lifelong learning abilities, Yuan Ze University (hereinafter referred as “YZU”) hereby establishes the “Regulations for the Implementation of the Disciplinary Self-Directed Learning Project” (hereinafter referred to as “the Regulations”).

Article 2 These Regulations encourage students to independently design personalized learning pathways within their respective academic disciplines based on their interests. According to the nature of each proposal, the project is categorized into four types:

1. Research Type: Students conduct diversified inquiries on specific topics, deepen their understanding of professional knowledge acquired from existing courses, or apply their knowledge to issue- or field-based practical learning projects.

2. Competition Type: Students participate in subject-specific or interdisciplinary competitions to enhance their expertise and practical skills, while also strengthening problem-solving and innovative thinking through competition experiences.

3. Certificate Type: Students formulate learning goals and execution strategies to participate in professional certification exams relevant to their academic or career development, thereby demonstrating the linkage between learning and professional growth.

4. Digital Learning Type: Students engage in self-directed learning via online platforms, flexibly managing their learning content and progress to broaden their global perspectives and stay informed of international trends.

Article 3 YZU establishes a Self-Directed and Interdisciplinary Learning Committee to oversee the planning and promotion of school-wide strategies related to professional and interdisciplinary learning. The Committee is convened by the Dean of Academic Affairs and comprises one faculty representative from each College, nominated by the respective Colleges. Each member serves a term of one year.

Article 4 Undergraduate students may apply individually or as a group of up to five members. However, for competition-oriented projects, if otherwise specified by the competition regulations, such rules shall apply.

Article 5 Students applying for research-, competition-, or certification-oriented projects must complete the “Introduction to Self-Directed Learning” course, invite a full-time faculty member to serve as a faculty advisor, and submit a written proposal in the designated format. Applications must be submitted to the Teaching Excellence Center, Office of Academic Affairs during the application period. Proposals will be reviewed by respective departments and the Self-Directed and Interdisciplinary Learning Committee. Students must submit a final report by the specified deadline. The Teaching Excellence Center will compile and forward the reports for final assessment by the departments and the Committee. Grades will be recorded as “Pass” or “Fail” according to the final assessment results.

## Article 6

Students applying for digital learning-oriented projects must select courses from the approved digital course list and submit application. A full-time faculty member must serve as the faculty advisor. At the end of the term, students must submit proof of course completion or a course certificate. Upon approval, students will be awarded elective credits. The International Academy will collect the applications and completion documents and submit them to the Self-Directed and Interdisciplinary Learning Committee for evaluation. Grades will be recorded as “Pass” or “Fail.”

Article 7 Each project may be awarded 1, 2, or 3 credits depending on its content and scope. As a general rule, 18 hours of learning is equivalent to 1 credit, which serves as the basis for credit recognition. Credits may not be duplicated under the following circumstances:

1. The project content overlaps with existing credited courses or has already been credited elsewhere.

2. The project consists of work from capstone projects, theses, or internships without independent innovation or extension.

3. When the content of multiple self-directed learning projects overlaps, only one project may be counted for credit.

A maximum of 3 credits may be counted toward free elective credits.

Article 8 Each department may formulate its own implementation guidelines based on its educational goals and shall submit them to the Office of Academic Affairs for record.

Article 9 These Regulations shall be implemented following approval by the Academic Affairs Meeting. Amendments shall follow the same procedure.
```
